MonitorTest flagged node-not-ready during intentional commatrix nftables reboot on SNO.
INFRA LOW
🆕 New issue
Full AI Analysis

PROJECT TESTS PASSED — failure is from CI framework


Test 1: [single-node-e2e-test] MonitorTest failure

• Duration: 2h0m46s
• Error: Suite run returned error: failed due to a MonitorTest failure
• Evidence:

```

Suite run returned error: failed due to a MonitorTest failure

error: error running a test suite: failed due to a MonitorTest failure

{"component":"entrypoint","error":"wrapped process failed: exit status 1",...,"msg":"Error executing test process","time":"2026-06-22T15:56:16Z"}

INFO[2026-06-22T15:56:17Z] Step aws-ovn-network-flow-matrix-single-node-single-node-e2e-test failed after 2h0m46s.

```

Commatrix test step confirmed passing beforehand:

```

INFO[2026-06-22T13:55:30Z] Step aws-ovn-network-flow-matrix-single-node-network-flow-matrix-tests succeeded after 9m35s.

{"timestamp":1782136529,"passed":true,"result":"SUCCESS","revision":"main"}

```

Node reboot triggered by commatrix nftables test at 13:50:

```

2026/06/22 13:50:22 Node ip-10-0-20-68.us-west-1.compute.internal is NotReady

STEP: Rebooting first node: ip-10-0-20-68.us-west-1.compute.internal and waiting for disconnect @ 06/22/26 13:50:04.659

```

MonitorTest interval collection spanned this window (13:17:35–15:54:10), catching the reboot-induced NotReady:

```

Processing monitorTest: apiserver-external-availability

finalIntervals size = 120703

first interval time: From = 2026-06-22 13:17:35 +0000 UTC

last interval time: From = 2026-06-22 15:54:10.245733205 +0000 UTC

```

• Root Cause: The commatrix nftables test (nftables_test.go) intentionally applies a MachineConfig to the SNO node and reboots it as part of verifying firewall rules after reboot. The node ip-10-0-20-68.us-west-1.compute.internal went NotReady at 13:50:22. The single-node-e2e-test CI framework step's openshift-tests suite was running MonitorTests (including apiserver-external-availability) that recorded the API server disruption during this intentional reboot and treated it as a test failure. The commatrix project's own 3 tests all passed and its finished.json reports "result":"SUCCESS".
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — this is a CI framework sensitivity issue, not a commatrix regression.
• Source File: https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/blob/release-4.21/test/e2e/nftables_test.go (line ~85, should apply firewall by blocking all ports except the ones OCP is listening on)
• Is it a flake? yes — the SNO reboot is intentional and deterministic; MonitorTest detecting node-not-ready during a deliberate reboot is a recurring pattern in SNO e2e jobs.
• Suggested Fix: Annotate or exempt the node-not-ready interval caused by the MachineConfig-driven reboot in the MonitorTest framework (e.g. add a disruption annotation before/after reboot, similar to how upgrade tests exempt planned reboots). No commatrix code change is needed.


TL;DR: MonitorTest flagged node-not-ready during intentional commatrix nftables reboot on SNO.


Relation Between Failures: There is exactly one failure chain: the commatrix nftables test intentionally rebooted the SNO node via MachineConfig to verify firewall rules, which caused a brief API server disruption; the CI framework's openshift-tests MonitorTest (apiserver-external-availability) captured this as a failure condition and caused the single-node-e2e-test step to exit 1. The commatrix project tests themselves all passed with SUCCESS.


Per-Version Notes:

• 4.21: Confirmed — MonitorTest failure on intentional SNO reboot in single-node-e2e-test step; commatrix tests passed.
• 4.22: Same root cause expected — identical job structure (aws-ovn-network-flow-matrix-single-node) with same nftables reboot step and same single-node-e2e-test MonitorTest wrapper.
• 5.0: Same root cause expected — same job topology; MonitorTest sensitivity to node-not-ready during planned reboots is a CI framework behavior not tied to OCP version.

Affected Images: ci/telco-runner:latest (test runner), registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-06-21-232046 (cluster under test). No image pull failures observed; all pipeline images tagged successfully.

❌ failure4.204.20-e2e-telco5g-ptp143minfra_other LOW
Dual NIC BC outage test timed out because `SKIP_INTERFACES` protected ptp4l.0.config's slave NIC, leaving one PTP path alive.
1 failed test
INFRA LOW
🆕 New issue
Full AI Analysis

Test 1: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP Outage recovery BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage [Serial]


• Duration: 391s (6m31s — 5m test timeout + ~1m30s BeforeEach overhead)
• Error: Timed out after 300.000s. expected clock class to degrade from Locked (6) after upstream link loss; Expected : false to be true
• Evidence:

```

ptp4l.0.config slave NIC (ens4f2) STILL receiving PTP sync throughout the test window:

[linuxptp-daemon-xkbd4] 2026-06-22T06:09:59.946654745Z ptp4l[14810.943]: [ptp4l.0.config:6] master offset -53 s2 freq -9304 path delay 2173


ptp4l.1.config slave NIC (ens2f1) recovered at test cleanup (DeferCleanup ran on timeout):

[linuxptp-daemon-xkbd4] 2026-06-22T06:13:48.524950754Z ptp4l[15039.522]: [ptp4l.1.config:5] port 1 (ens2f1): FAULTY to LISTENING on INIT_COMPLETE


log_parsing.go explicitly rejects non-SLAVE→X transitions:

E0622 06:13:48.524856 298661 log_parsing.go:65] Failed to extract metrics from ptp4l output: unrecognized role in event: FAULTY to LISTENING on INIT_COMPLETE

```

• Root Cause: portEngine.TurnAllPortsDown(skipInterfaces) had ptp4l.0.config's NIC (ens4f2) in SKIP_INTERFACES to prevent cluster disconnection. Only ptp4l.1.config's ens2f1 was brought down. With ptp4l.0.config continuing to receive PTP sync from the GM (s2/SLAVE state confirmed in daemon logs throughout 06:08–06:13), the Dual NIC BC maintained a live upstream path and clock class never degraded from 6. The openshift_ptp_clock_class{config="ptp4l.0.config"} metric — the one the test reads — stayed at 6 the entire 5-minute window. This is an infra configuration mismatch: the cluster management NIC overlaps with a PTP slave NIC, making a true all-links-down outage test impossible on this hardware.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Introduced in test commit [ccd1e711](https://github.com/openshift/ptp-operator/commit/ccd1e711) (2026-04-20) "test: Replace RecoverySlaveNetworkOutage with PortEngine". The new PortEngine-based implementation requires SKIP_INTERFACES, which the old implementation did not. On this telco bare-metal setup (cnfdf30/cnfdf31/cnfdf32), the skipped interface is a PTP slave NIC, preventing full outage simulation.
• Source File: [test/conformance/serial/ptp.go L2121–L2190](https://github.com/openshift/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go#L2121-L2190)
• Is it a flake? No — deterministic failure on this hardware. The SKIP_INTERFACES value on this cluster always includes ptp4l.0.config's upstream NIC, so the full outage is never achieved and the test always times out.
• Suggested Fix: Update the CI step configuration (or node annotation) so SKIP_INTERFACES only lists the true management/bond interface, not a PTP slave NIC. Alternatively, configure one of the PTP slave NICs to use a separate physical interface that is not part of the cluster management path.


TL;DR: Dual NIC BC outage test timed out because SKIP_INTERFACES protected ptp4l.0.config's slave NIC, leaving one PTP path alive.


Relation Between Failures: There is only one failing test. Its failure is entirely self-contained: SKIP_INTERFACES on the cnfdf30 bare-metal node prevents a complete upstream link outage, so the BC clock class never degrades from 6 and the 5-minute Eventually assertion times out. No other test on the cluster was affected.


Per-Version Notes:

• OCP 4.20 (nightly-2026-06-21-183852): One test failure in dualnicbc-serial outage recovery suite. All other 140 tests (bc, dualfollower, oc, tgm suites) passed.

Affected Images:

• image-registry.openshift-image-registry.svc:5000/openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon:4.20
• image-registry.openshift-image-registry.svc:5000/openshift-ptp/ptp-operator:4.20
• image-registry.openshift-image-registry.svc:5000/openshift-ptp/cloud-event-proxy:4.20

❌ failure4.234.23-e2e-telco5g-ptp-upstream165minfra_other LOW
All 147 PTP tests passed; job failed because post-phase gather steps got Unauthorized from the API server.
INFRA LOW
🆕 New issue
Full AI Analysis

PROJECT TESTS PASSED — failure is from CI framework


The telco5g-ptp-tests step completed with "passed":true,"result":"SUCCESS" (finished.json) and all 147 executed tests passed (0 failures, 0 errors per test_results.json). No PTP-operator or linuxptp-daemon test failed.


The job-level failure originated in the post phase, specifically in the gather-extra and gather-audit-logs CI steps, which could not authenticate to the cluster API server. Verbatim evidence from ci-operator-build-log.txt:



error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)
error completing cluster type inspection: error running backup collection: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials
error getting cluster version: Unauthorized
ClusterVersion: Installing "" for <unknown>: <unknown>
error: creating temp namespace: Unauthorized
Step e2e-telco5g-ptp-upstream-gather-audit-logs failed after 11s.
Step phase post failed after 15m7s.

The cluster API server returned Unauthorized for every request the gather containers made (oc adm inspect, log fetching, namespace creation). This caused both post-step containers to exit with code 1, which ci-operator converted into a job-level failure (executing_graph:step_failed:executing_multi_stage_test). The suspicious ClusterVersion: Installing "" for suggests the cluster may have been in a partially degraded or re-installing state by the time the post phase ran, invalidating the CI service-account credentials used by the gather steps.



TL;DR: All 147 PTP tests passed; job failed because post-phase gather steps got Unauthorized from the API server.


Relation Between Failures: Both gather-extra and gather-audit-logs failed for exactly the same reason — the cluster API server was returning Unauthorized to the CI service account at the time the post phase executed (≈07:30–07:45 UTC). Neither failure has any connection to PTP-operator code; they are sequential post-steps that both hit the same expired/invalidated credential state.


Per-Version Notes: OCP 4.23 nightly (4.23.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-065515) — cluster API auth degraded in post-phase; all project tests passed on this nightly build.


Affected Images: registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.23.0-0.nightly-2026-06-20-065515 (cluster under test); ci/telco-runner:latest (gather step runner). No PTP-operator or linuxptp-daemon images were affected.

❌ failure5.05.0-e2e-telco5g-ptp372mtest_failure

🆕 New issue
Full AI Analysis

Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence: Same pmc bad-command pattern as Test 4; here getClockIDViaPMC(pod, configFile, "grandmasterIdentity") is called via GetClockIDMaster fallback path
• Root Cause: Same as Test 4 — BC in FREERUN + getClockIDViaPMC buggy separate-arg pmc call
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No (same as Test 4)
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 6: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 202s
• Error: parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.0.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence/Root Cause/Fix: Same as Test 4 (different config index .0 vs .1, same failure mode)
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:

• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence: Same pmc bad-command pattern as Test 4; here getClockIDViaPMC(pod, configFile, "grandmasterIdentity") is called via GetClockIDMaster fallback path
• Root Cause: Same as Test 4 — BC in FREERUN + getClockIDViaPMC buggy separate-arg pmc call
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No (same as Test 4)
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 6: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 202s
• Error: parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.0.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence/Root Cause/Fix: Same as Test 4 (different config index .0 vs .1, same failure mode)
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4

• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence: Same pmc bad-command pattern as Test 4; here getClockIDViaPMC(pod, configFile, "grandmasterIdentity") is called via GetClockIDMaster fallback path
• Root Cause: Same as Test 4 — BC in FREERUN + getClockIDViaPMC buggy separate-arg pmc call
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No (same as Test 4)
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

• Duration: 202s

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

• Is it a flake? No
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence: Same pmc bad-command pattern as Test 4; here getClockIDViaPMC(pod, configFile, "grandmasterIdentity") is called via GetClockIDMaster fallback path
• Root Cause: Same as Test 4 — BC in FREERUN + getClockIDViaPMC buggy separate-arg pmc call
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No (same as Test 4)
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

• Duration: 202s
• Error: parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.0.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence/Root Cause/Fix: Same as Test 4 (different config index .0 vs .1, same failure mode)
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4

• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence: Same pmc bad-command pattern as Test 4; here getClockIDViaPMC(pod, configFile, "grandmasterIdentity") is called via GetClockIDMaster fallback path
• Root Cause: Same as Test 4 — BC in FREERUN + getClockIDViaPMC buggy separate-arg pmc call
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No (same as Test 4)
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 6: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 202s
• Error: parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.0.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence/Root Cause/Fix: Same as Test 4 (different config index .0 vs .1, same failure mode)
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:

• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
• Evidence: Same pmc bad-command pattern as Test 4; here getClockIDViaPMC(pod, configFile, "grandmasterIdentity") is called via GetClockIDMaster fallback path
• Root Cause: Same as Test 4 — BC in FREERUN + getClockIDViaPMC buggy separate-arg pmc call
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go
• Is it a flake? No (same as Test 4)
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 4

• Duration: 202s

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 7: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock [Serial]

• Duration: 300s
• Error: PMC clock class 248 (FREERUN) for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config; expected 6 (LOCKED)
• Evidence: Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config. Expected : 248 to equal : 6 — pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET actually succeeded here (using GetClockClassViaPMC which correctly passes "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" as one arg) and returned clock class 248. Clock class 248 = FREERUN in IEEE 1588.
• Root Cause: The BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN because its upstream grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is not providing a locked clock signal (class 6). This is direct hardware/sync evidence that the GM is not locked. The BC cannot propagate a class it has never received.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknow


Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the full analysis:



Test 1: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: No Follower port in LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1; ens2f0np0 clock state metric not found
• Evidence: ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state, nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found, available op[...] — the Prometheus metric for ens2f0np0 doesn't exist, meaning ptp4l on cnfdf31 never advertised a clock state for that interface. Earlier in the build log: [testconfig.go: 1817] ptptConfig: test-bc-master1, masterIfCount: 1, slaveIfCount: 1 — BC discovered but sync-dependent.
• Root Cause: The upstream BC (test-bc-master1, cnfdf32) is in FREERUN (not locked to GM), so the slave on cnfdf31 stays in LISTENING state on ens2f0np0. The linuxptp-daemon only publishes openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics for interfaces that have entered SLAVE state; LISTENING interfaces produce no metric entry. The slave waits 600 s for a LOCKED metric that never appears.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — likely the same GM FREERUN root cause shared with Tests 7/22; see those entries.
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go
• Is it a flake? Possibly — if the GM hardware simply hadn't acquired GNSS lock in time. But clock class 248 persisted for the full 3h45m test run, suggesting a non-transient hardware or configuration failure.
• Suggested Fix: Determine why the grandmaster (test-grandmaster) is in FREERUN (check ts2phc/GNSS logs). Verify that openshift_ptp_clock_state metrics are published even for LISTENING interfaces so the test can detect that state explicitly.

Test 2: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: Same as Test 1 — no LOCKED state for test-slave1, ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing
• Evidence: Same verbatim error pattern as Test 1 for ens2f0np0 on cnfdf31
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1 — BC in FREERUN cascades to LISTENING slave; ens2f0np0 metric absent
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 3: [dualfollower-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Can provide a profile with higher priority [Serial]

• Duration: 600s
• Error: ens2f3np3 role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) + ens2f0np0 clock state metric missing for ptpconfig temp
• Evidence: ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) — ens2f3np3 is explicitly in LISTENING state, confirming that ptp4l is running BMCA without a reachable locked master. ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: ... aIf: ens2f0np0 not found
• Root Cause: Same as Test 1. The "higher priority profile" test installs a temporary ptpconfig (name=temp) and expects the slave to re-sync; because the BC/GM is in FREERUN, the slave never leaves LISTENING on either interface.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Same as Test 1
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go
• Is it a flake? Same as Test 1
• Suggested Fix: Same as Test 1

Test 4: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Slave can sync to master [Serial]

• Duration: 204s
• Error: pmc GET PARENT_DATA_SET returns "bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET" for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

This comes from getClockIDViaPMC in the test runner image (cloned from k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator main, commit 3b93c9f4): []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} — "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" are passed as two separate argv elements. The linuxptp pmc binary calls run_pmc_command() on each remaining arg individually; "GET" alone (no TLV name) and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone (no action verb) are both invalid, producing two "bad command" lines.

• Root Cause: Two compounding issues: (1) Primary — ptp4l on the BC (cnfdf32, test-bc-master1) is in FREERUN (no locked GM), so it never logs "selected best master clock", causing GetClockIDForeign log-parsing to time out after 1 minute and fall back to getClockIDViaPMC. (2) Secondary — getClockIDViaPMC introduced in upstream commit 3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026) is buggy: it passes "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as separate pmc args instead of a single "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string, producing "bad command" errors from pmc.
• Breaking PR/Commit: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/commit/3b93c9f4 (Jun 9, 2026 — "tests: add retries to PTP clock ID lookups")
• Source File: https://github.com/k8snetworkplumbingwg/ptp-operator/blob/main/test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go (line ~133)
• Is it a flake? No for the pmc bug (deterministic code defect). The BC FREERUN component may be hardware-related.
• Suggested Fix: In getClockIDViaPMC, change []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET", "PARENT_DATA_SET"} to []string{"pmc", "-b", "0", "-u", "-f", configFile, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET"} (single combined arg) so pmc receives the full command string as one argv element.

Test 5: [dualnicbc-serial] PTP e2e tests PTP ClockSync Downstream slave can sync to BC master [Serial]

• Duration: 203s
• Error: grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET
